In terms of utensils, such as Samsung mosquito coils, Huasheng electric fans, Lihe brand washbasins, laundry basins, Huafu straw hats, and Wuzhou Yalin anti-epidemic water. In terms of diet, such as Yantai beer, Yili soda, and Guansheng cold food canned food. These many well-known and popular national products have long been happily used by society, so there is no need to describe them one by one. However, at the end of this article, the author hopes with the greatest enthusiasm that all compatriots in the country, in the present situation where private goods are flooding the country and dumping goods wildly, must not eat the small cheapness, and leave behind the hatred of destroying the country, but should urgently love national products, develop industry and commerce, and save the crisis of the dying national economy.

The Light of National Products

Talking About the Efficacy of Tianli Ammonia 185

— Xin Fu

Clerks working in writing rooms, because they work at their desks from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM, feel uncomfortable in body and mind, and their minds are dizzy and extremely tired. In this situation, if you just smell the ammonia a little, then you can immediately refresh your mind and turn into an energetic person. Working can achieve the effect of "doing more with less effort." It is the only stimulant that does not stimulate the heart or hurt the nervous system.

When bathing with "Tianli Ammonia," the whole body is dirty and can be washed thoroughly, and the skin is smooth, and you feel exceptionally comfortable. On the one hand, it can increase the skin's resistance... In the hot summer, every family cannot do without it.

Household ammonia is especially liked by people with beards. Because ammonia can gradually soften the beard, and it can also reduce the number of shavings. Also, when the shaving blade is blunt, just soak it in Tianli Ammonia for a few seconds, and then wipe it dry, then the blade will be as sharp as new.

Adding half a grid of ammonia to the hot water in the foot basin, soaking and washing it before going to bed can make you feel comfortable and fall asleep. It can be said to be an essential medicine for people suffering from insomnia.

After being bitten by mosquitoes or poisonous insects, immediately apply ammonia, which can relieve pain, detoxify and reduce swelling in an instant.

Pour half a grid of "Tianli Ammonia" (do not mix with water) in the room to make the air clean. If it is in a sick room, then you can avoid the transmission of bacteria.

Everyone knows that plants can regulate gas and carbonic acid gas, and flowers can make people feel happy and have a pleasant feeling, so plants and flowers seem to have a close relationship that cannot be separated from human life. But how should we protect it? That is to mix a little ammonia with a gallon of water to irrigate the roots of plants and flowers, watering it twice a week (do not interrupt).

Using "Tianli Ammonia" to wash silk and woolen fabrics has the following special effects: Does not turn yellow, does not fade, has a lovely luster, does not damage the material, is easy to dry, and does not shrink.

Ammonia also has a great effect on women's hair washing. It can remove all the grease and dirt from the hair and make it shiny and lustrous. Used for laundry, "it removes dirt and dirt far better than soap," and it saves all kinds of trouble, which is more convenient than using soap powder.

"Bright windows and clean desks" This is how clean and happy a family is. As for how to make the windows bright and the desks clean? Then it is to apply "Tianli Ammonia" which will definitely guarantee your "satisfaction."

There are many other uses, but I can't describe them all one by one here due to space limitations. I hope that compatriots in the country will buy more "excellent national products" so that the national industry can be fully developed, and on the one hand, the national economy can be enriched through the efforts of several national products manufacturers and the people's adoption as much as possible.

Lake Writings 187

— Chen Cuina

Boating

Light rain has a sunny intent, the lake and sky are blue at a glance, the water is deep and the oars are heavy, the duckweed is full and the fish are abundant, spring bamboo shoots suddenly grow tall, white clouds close to a hermitage, compose poems and live as you please, do not be greedy for obtaining sentences.

I occasionally said that I lived in West Lake, and the second brother echoed, saying, I haven't left the house for years, just to complete a poem.

Living in West Lake, I haven't left the house, grass grows and the secluded path is narrow, people are quiet and birds are noisy, the wild water is so green, the white lotus is naturally fragrant, in the evening a pot of wine, also next to the apricot flower village.

Frog Sounds in the Wild Water 188

— Shu Fan

After a heavy rain all night, the curtain waves are like snow. I vaguely think that in the recorded place of rice fields, the frog sounds should be shaking with anger. My hometown has a saying, "Many frogs mean the rice is ripe, and much rain makes the silkworm women cry." The frogs can eat the locust nymphs, and the farmers verify the abundance of the harvest by the tiny insects, which is more reliable than the divination of the gods. Therefore, I made a law for myself, and the prohibition of capture is very strict. Every time at the turn of spring and summer, I let them play in the ponds and wild waters. Fortunately, they are competing with bream and carp to ascend the knife and chopping board. The canals and banks in Shanghai are filled, and the aquatic plants are all lost. This sound is no longer available. Only in the remote fields, passing by under the moon, can I still vaguely hear it in my ears. It should be said that frogs are also one of the migratory insects, calling for spring farming, no less than the cricket urging the lazy woman. Once a year, the people's livelihood is depended on. However, the bustling city is floating and frivolous, indulging in erotic songs and drowning in decadent sounds. Who knows that more than ten miles away, there is this sound of nature? Is it not sad that for a long time it has been abandoned, and that people are ignorant of farming and do not care about it?

Frogs respond to the agricultural season, and also cooperate with ancient poems: "Artemisia is full of the ground, and the buds are short," this is when the tadpoles are active; "Peach blossoms are gone and rape flowers are yellow," then it is when the ponds are noisy. After the new rain has just stopped, the wet moon flows yellow, so that sitting in a virtual hall and listening quietly, all the sounds from near and far respond to each other, like a noisy drum, warning and competing; if the general's order is strict, the soldiers are angry and strong; its spirit is majestic, its sound is strong, and it cannot be compared with the autumn insects' taste of sorrow and coolness. Therefore, seeing that at night after finishing class by the window, enjoying the complex sounds, throwing down the pen and making a color, I am self-righteous, not counting Zu Sheng hearing the rooster crow. Now that the world has been fed, and the spring dreams have all awakened, and I am staying by the lake, hearing this sound and stroking my head, all kinds of feelings gather: the seasons flow around, my ambition has not been fulfilled, I sit and watch the remnant lamp flowers, and I sigh and ask what to do!

Although frogs are insects, they have a habitat, and they are quiet at night, not worrying about being attacked, which is close to skill. Frogs that are floating on the algae are colored, and frogs that are spotted are padded on the bank or tree roots, concealing themselves, and blinding the eyes, which is close to wisdom. If they are angry, they will stimulate the decadent energy, and then they will be great courage. In this bleak autumn of storms, how can we capture ten thousand angry frogs and divide them into the corridors, so that those who are like King Yue can use them as a model, and those who have courage among the scholars and commoners can be moved by them and rise up, and perhaps there is something that can be done!

Shen Yishi in Jiangwan raises frogs the most. He opened up land and built a house, surrounded by fences, and three ponds in the middle. Except for the thin planting of flowers and plants on the shore, the reed water is full of green-bellied and green-backed toads. When it is sunny, there are cloud shadows and sky light, pouring into the blue waves, and the frogs are swimming or jumping, scattering into the remaining beauty. He sighs at the wonderful taste of Hao Liang, and it is not more than this. At night, the dark flowers bear dew, and the water surface is slightly eroded, as if dense stars are swallowed, and they are shaking their tongues and stirring up waves. I have been to his place twice, and I have enjoyed all the pleasures. There are species collected from the Americas, so large that they are comparable to crouching civets, and Westerners are sold happily, each pair can earn more than five gold. The feed can find its own aquatic insects, without the need for feeding. In ancient times, there were those who played with cranes to the end of their lives, and this is hidden in frogs. Building a house in the human realm, without the disturbance of cars and horses, although it is said to be secluded and barren, there are also trumpets, so why must you leave the deep mountains and bid farewell to the secular world before you can get it?

Trip to Qingyang Port 189

— Zhu Ying

On a Sunday morning, I followed friends to Qingyang Port to watch the dragon boat races, hoping to dispel the accumulated boredom from long seclusion in the city.

The weather that day was neither cold nor too hot; truly, one could say the sky was clear and the breeze gentle. Advancing in the light of the rising sun, chatting and laughing, the wheels had already left Shanghai and plunged into the embrace of nature. The expanse of green outside the car window drew our gaze, the yellow wheat waves breaking through all the gray impressions in our minds, startling us with the realization that the season had turned to wheat harvesting and rice planting.

The wheels mechanically rolled past several stations, finally spitting us out of the carriage at our destination. It was quite surprising; there were already many gentlemen and ladies wandering by the river and in the fields. Ah, perhaps these were people who had escaped from the city at the first opportunity to spend their so-called weekends in this place. Indeed, even in this rural area, there are "hotel" like places for noble gentlemen and ladies to rest their horses and feet.

Our group of three, all pretending to be poets, lay in the wheat waves for a while, sat under the green shade for a while, and strolled along the Qingyang Port, heads bowed. The sun shone through the transparent air, and the three of us took several deep breaths, inhaling the fresh air that cost nothing.

The dragon boat race began. Ten boats advanced with drums and music in the calm Qingyang Port, earning applause from the audience on both sides of the river. Even more so, a group of nearly twenty female students jumped with rhythmic steps, encouraging the rowers with rhythmic tunes to move forward, to strive forward.

At noon, we ate at a small rural restaurant, consuming fresh fish and shrimp, which, although simple and unadorned, tasted very delicious. Old Hu, who was with us, spent one yuan in legal currency to buy two large carp and a pound of lively fresh shrimp to take home to his wife as proof of his trip.

After the meal, we strolled around the countryside for a while, and a little before three o'clock, we climbed back into the belly of the train. Quite coincidentally, those nearly twenty female students were also riding in this carriage. With nearly twenty lively and beautiful angels in one carriage, the air was filled with a rosy atmosphere.

Crisp laughter, mixed with the beautiful songs of famous English tunes, drew the attention of all the passengers to a corner of the carriage where more than a dozen large straw hats floated.

The train advanced rhythmically in the soft sunlight, and before we knew it, it had slowly been pulled into the platform of the Shanghai North Station.

Water Carrier of Taihu Lake 190

— Photograph by Zhang Zhenhou

Journey to the Water Towns 191

— Chen Liang

Both banks are deep green, and the water is also deep green. The long, flowing water carries finely woven duckweed, slowly following the June wind, floating past my eyes and disappearing behind me.

"Aren't people like duckweed, drifting on the surface of the world?" I don't know where this piercing question came from. Looking at the curved banks and the villages hidden in the dense shade, sitting on the bow of the boat, puffing out faint smoke rings, a sense of茫然 and flow of the water, washed over me. Wild roses laughed on the shore, white and pink, but the withered flowers, petal after petal, fell on the mud by the water, forever burying its color, its fragrance, its everything that was pleasing……

So, I dare not turn my head to look at Terry in the cabin. She is a woman who has been trampled on by life in the dusty world, with the color of wild roses, the fragrance of wild roses, but these days will probably not last long, blown by the great wind of life into the mud-like destiny, forever burying her.

The weeping willows gently brushed the water, and three or five village children, ignoring the mud over their knees, were exploring for their beloved fresh treasures, only a few small crabs. That kind of smile moved my fragile heartstrings. Doesn't the world have many people who spend their whole lives treading in the mud to seek the true meaning of life?——In the June wind, the boat slowly turned around the bend.

Again, long green banks, again, long green water, again, duckweed floating by.

But I felt the loneliness of the water towns. Terry was singing the enthusiastic "Indian Folk Song" in the cabin. Unexpectedly, she even showed a smile that didn't know bitterness. Quietly, she lit another cigarette, took a puff, two puffs...smoking, not caring about the boatman behind, who knows where he was rowing us to.

Comfortable Sleeping Chair 192

— Wang Ji

The Mated Luan and Phoenix Replaced 193

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Light Rain and Slanting Wind Still Leave Traces; Silent Night, Writing a Letter of Severance

When he ran into her, his attitude was very comfortable and he didn't look like a sick person. But he didn't have an angry look, and he didn't seem to be angry with anyone. This girl's attitude has to be said to be unpredictable. During this week, he had another way to solve this difficulty. It turned out that he had used this courage on the tip of his pen and written a letter, which he sent to Luo Lan's school. When Menglan went to school, the gatekeeper sent the letter over. She saw a layered, printed envelope with a very delicate handwriting on it: Miss Jiang Menglan, Zhenkun Girls' School, kindly opened. The signature below read: Zhang Jian, this city. As soon as Menglan saw it, she couldn't help but feel a flurry of excitement in her heart. She said, "This is a letter from the Women's Normal School. Miss Zhang didn't come, she's writing a letter for fun." Saying this, she looked around to see if anyone was around, quickly took the letter and walked to a quiet place on campus. Seeing that no one was nearby, she sat on a short railing under a clump of banana trees, with her back to the pedestrians, and read the letter. The letter read:

Miss Menglan: I am suddenly presumptuous to send you this letter. I know I am being presumptuous. However, in today's society, with the advancement of culture, male and female interactions are seen as equal, which is common in Western customs. You are studying at a school run by Westerners, so you may excuse my behavior by Western customs; however, my admiration is sincere. I am not talented, and I earn a living by writing to support my mother. I know I am mediocre and not valued by the literati. But for the past two months, every time I meet you on the road, I feel as if I am bathed in the clear air of the light wind and misty moon. I don't know why, but I feel like a sunflower facing the sun, unable to suppress my inclination. However, I have only caught a glimpse and have not yet asked you directly. Later, I saw you holding a popular magazine with my humble writings published on the cover. I then realized that my shallow works have long been appreciated by your discerning eyes. In ancient times, people who found a confidant could die without regret. I dare not insult your orchid-like qualities by calling you a confidante. However, I admire you and cannot remain silent. Also, I thought that a cautious person like me could not express my feelings. I was worried and didn't know what to do. A few days ago, I visited a distant relative who has a younger sister studying at your school. Accidentally, I read the yearbook of your school at her home. Your beautiful photo and name were both there. So I was able to take advantage of this postal route to present this short letter. If you can forgive my rashness and allow me to correspond with you, then we can exchange ideas and improve each other's writing between the paper and ink. My words are sincere, and I dare not hope for anything else. I happened to collect a line from an ancient poem: "I am a melancholy guest in this world, meeting you again in the season of falling flowers." This feeling, this scene, the fourteen characters cannot express all that I feel, so this letter has lingered in my mind for two days and nights, half-written and placed in my bosom for another day and night, and finally I sent it. Even if I offend you, I have no choice, right? Respectfully presented, I am anxiously awaiting your reply. Zhang Guoqi (42)

Miscellaneous thoughts

Random Thoughts on Rural Living 194

— Ziwei

There are many people who are constantly advocating "going to the countryside." However, if you pay attention to where they live, they are still living in magnificent Western-style houses on some street, which is the same ridiculous thing as friends who promote domestic products every day, but wear imported Western suits themselves.

In truth, the air in the countryside is too good, but unfortunately, transportation is ultimately inconvenient. If you are a solitary person who doesn't like being enthusiastic, living there is very suitable. However, good air cannot be exchanged for bread. Now, the real rural people always want to run to the city.

I have been living in the countryside for about two years, and I don't feel any inconvenience in my habits. My frail body has actually become stronger, which proves the benefits of nature in the countryside being suitable for human life. Take the mosquitoes in the summer, for example, they are much stronger than those in the city. And their activity time is also longer. The buzzing of the mosquito swarm starts in May and won't be heard until the end of October. If I hadn't prepared the Invincible brand mosquito incense from the family industry cooperative last year, then perhaps I would have "returned to the city" long ago.

Last summer, one rainy day, the Invincible brand was used up, and I bought two new brands. I really suffered for a whole night without being able to close my eyes. Some of our neighbors use mosquito nets, but they are still useless. Some light locally made mosquito smoke sticks, which are very strong, and people cough when they smell them, so now they have also switched to the inexpensive and high-quality Invincible brand.

These days, it's the season of the mold, and the weather is so humid. For someone with my kind of heavy moisture, my stomach often feels sluggish. I usually like to drink light tea, but these days, I don't dare to drink light tea because I consulted a doctor who said that light tea is most likely to generate moisture. It accumulates over time and you don't feel it much. As long as the humid season comes, drinking light tea, especially for someone with a moist body, will make it even worse.

But for someone who is used to drinking tea, it's as if they have a very hard time if they don't touch their lips to water all day long. Moreover, I often have to run around in the hot sun. After sweating like crazy, my throat feels even more thirsty. The doctor told me to use Job's tears and tangerine peel instead of tea, but it's not very palatable and doesn't quench my thirst. For example, drinking plain boiled water seems bland and tasteless, and chrysanthemum and black tea don't suit my taste. It's funny, but it seems very difficult to solve this small drinking problem.

The year before last, my wife bought two bottles of fruit juice. The taste was sweet and fragrant. When mixed with cold boiled water, it was very thirst-quenching. I drank it a few times and my appetite felt better. Later, one summer, I didn't want to eat any cold drinks (because of the moisture, eating soda or ice cream would make my stomach feel sluggish and sick). I specialized in eating fruit juice, with the feeling that "I can't live without this gentleman for a day."

Over the past two or three years, I can distinguish the good and bad of fruit juice very clearly. Among them, those that don't mix saccharin and don't use raw water, and don't dry out my throat after eating, I trust the Guanshengyuan brand as more pure in domestic products, because imported goods are too expensive. If you are greedy for cheapness, you will inevitably buy things with saccharin and raw water.

Now, summer has arrived again. Although I live in a remote and poor countryside, for me, mosquito incense and fruit juice are indispensable and must be bought early.

Special Telegram Supplement

Please Governmental and Military Institutions Comply with the Executive Yuan's Order to Collect Cash for Official Telegrams 227

— Zhen

Recently, the Executive Yuan stipulated three measures to rectify the fees for official military telegrams: 1. Starting from July 1, 1936, the "Regulations on Fees and Restrictions for Official Military Telegrams of the National Government" should be strictly enforced. 2. A circular order should be issued to all military and political institutions to restrict the sending of telegrams, and those who abuse telegrams under the guise of official institutions for personal gain should be severely punished. 3. If senders do not comply with the aforementioned regulations and forcibly demand that telegrams be sent, the relevant responsible authorities should severely punish them after investigation. The above measures have been circulated to all institutions for compliance and have been printed and posted. Will the collection of cash for official telegrams achieve its intended purpose from now on?

The expenses of the telegraph administration rely solely on telegram fees. In recent years, due to the suppression of bandits, many new telegraph lines have been established, resulting in large and insufficient expenditures. In addition, the arrears of official military telegrams are very heavy. From the establishment of the capital by the National Government in 1928 to the end of 1935, the accumulated arrears have reached more than 37 million yuan! If this continues, not only will public communications be unable to be maintained, but also military communications will be difficult to sustain. According to regulations, official military telegrams should be forwarded as a priority, and unless otherwise specified, the price should be half the ordinary rate for both clear and coded text telegrams. For military telegrams in combat or bandit suppression areas, the material fee is five jiao per hundred characters, and if the number of characters is less than one hundred, it should be counted as one hundred characters. These were stipulated in Articles 3 and 19 of the "Regulations on Fees and Restrictions for Official Military Telegrams" promulgated by the National Government in July 1934, and should be followed accordingly. However, due to frequent military operations and exhausted military funds, and with the arrears of official telegrams becoming a habit, while many political and military institutions pay for official military telegrams according to regulations, there are also many who repeatedly delay payment. Now, under the leadership of the supreme leader Mr. Chiang Kai-shek, the entire country's military and political affairs are increasing administrative efficiency and developing transportation functions as its policy guidelines, which is more powerful and has more achievements than any previous era. Therefore, it is certain that rectifying the fees for official military telegrams can be easily implemented effectively. The above measures are truly beneficial to the future of the telegraph industry.

Collecting cash for official telegrams is not only beneficial to the telegraph industry but also provides many conveniences for military and political institutions. Here are some further explanations:

Advancing Communication Speed: The value of telegrams lies in speed. Official military telegrams particularly value speed. However, the capacity of telegraph machines is limited, and the condition of the lines varies. Therefore, telegrams should be as brief as possible, and non-urgent matters should not be sent by telegram. Unnecessary words should not be included in the telegram text. In other words, sending fewer non-urgent telegrams will prevent the congestion of lines for urgent telegrams, and using fewer unnecessary words will speed up the transmission of necessary words. Recognizing this, Commander-in-Chief Chiang issued an order in December 1932 to the political and military institutions and bandit suppression troops in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui to strictly limit the sending of telegrams. "In the future, regardless of which institution sends a telegram, the text must be concise and clear. Unless it is absolutely necessary, it should not exceed one hundred characters. Non-urgent matters should not be marked with 'Urgent' unnecessarily. For non-emergency situations, express mail should be used instead of sending telegrams at every turn." Sending too many telegrams not only congests the lines but also delays important telegrams. It is hoped that political and military leaders will strictly comply with this order to avoid delaying matters.

Reducing Telegram Budget: Political and military institutions often overspend on telegrams due to the abuse of sending telegrams. As a result, the budget for telegrams is often too large and cannot be fully claimed. If the above measures are followed and strictly enforced for telegrams sent, telegram fees will be reduced. Moreover, if each telegram sent must be paid in cash according to regulations, the monthly telegram expenses can be clearly settled. In the future, it will not be difficult to determine the telegram budget, and it will not be difficult to audit the final accounts. Since the Executive Yuan has issued an order to pay for official military telegrams in cash, the political and military institutions can submit monthly requests for the telegram expenses they have incurred, and there will be no risk of arrears.

The greatest efficiency of a political organization lies in flexible operation, especially in orderly systems and effective implementation of orders. Now that President Chiang has the greatest determination to rectify the fees for official telegrams, it is hoped that all political and military institutions will strictly comply with President Chiang's intentions and strive to implement them to achieve effectiveness. Increasing administrative efficiency is indeed the goal, not only for the sake of the telegraph industry's future.

Discussing Ship Radio Telegrams 228

— Zhi

Telegrams transmitted between ship radio stations and coastal radio stations or other ship radio stations are called ship radio telegrams. Any ship that has been registered with the Ministry of Transportation and Communications and issued a ship radio station license may install its own radio telegraph equipment and communicate directly with the coastal radio stations under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Transportation and Communications. Telegrams exchanged between the above-mentioned ship radio stations and various locations within the country are called domestic ship telegrams. Ship telegrams that do not comply with the above regulations are considered international ship telegrams. Domestic ship telegrams are charged in national currency, and the fee per word is composed of three items: domestic fee, coastal radio station fee, and ship radio station fee. For example, according to the current domestic ship radio station rate table, the domestic fee and coastal radio station fee for ordinary or political rotary telegrams in Chinese clear language between ships and various locations within the country are both one jiao per word, and the ship radio station fee is five fen. Therefore, the total price per word is two jiao five fen. The total price per word for urgent telegrams in Chinese clear language is three jiao five fen. (Because the domestic fee for urgent telegrams is charged at twice the domestic fee for ordinary telegrams, the domestic fee for urgent telegrams in Chinese clear language should be two jiao per word, plus the coastal radio station fee of one jiao and the ship radio station fee of five fen, totaling three jiao five fen.) International ship telegrams are charged in gold francs, but within the national border, they may be charged in national currency according to the Ministry of Transportation and Communications' exchange rate between gold francs and national currency. The total price per word is composed of four items: ship radio station fee, coastal radio station fee, domestic telegraph line fee, and international telegraph line fee. For example, for telegrams between ships and Hong Kong, transmitted through the Ministry of Transportation and Communications' coastal radio station, domestic landline or radio, and the international radio circuit directly to Hong Kong, the total price per word should be 1.90 gold francs (but if the ship sends a telegram to Hong Kong from the Ministry of Transportation and Communications' coastal radio stations in Shanghai or Fuzhou, the price is only 1.40 gold francs per word, because this telegram does not pass through domestic lines, so the domestic telegraph line fee of 0.50 gold francs is deducted). Within the national border, the above-mentioned gold franc telegram rates are converted into national currency at the current exchange rate of 1.14 yuan per gold franc and 1.60 yuan per 1.40 gold francs.

According to Article 3 of the current "Ship Radio Telegram Fee Regulations," any ship that has not been registered with the Ministry of Transportation and Communications and issued a ship radio station license, if it communicates with the Ministry of Transportation and Communications' coastal radio stations, all exchanged telegrams should be charged as international ship telegrams. For example, suppose there are two ships equipped with ship radio stations, both sending Chinese clear language ship telegrams from Guangzhou to Nanjing at the same time. If one ship has not been registered with the Ministry of Transportation and Communications and issued a ship radio station license, the ship telegrams sent by that ship should be charged as international ship telegrams according to regulations, and the fee should be 1.40 gold francs per word, equivalent to 1.60 yuan in national currency. If the ship has been registered with the Ministry of Transportation and Communications and issued a license, the fee will be charged according to the domestic ship telegram rate, which is only 0.25 yuan per word, a significant difference. Therefore, all state-owned or foreign shipping companies can first apply to the Ministry of Transportation and Communications for registration of their ships, apply for a ship's nationality certificate, and then apply to the Radio Administration of the Ministry of Transportation and Communications to fill out and issue a ship radio station license before requesting the application of domestic ship telegram rates. After completing the above procedures, they can save a considerable amount of telegram fees each year. Therefore, all shipping companies should handle ship registration and ship radio station license application matters in accordance with regulations, without any hesitation.

Since the implementation of the "Domestic Telegraph Business Regulations," the "Ship Radio Telegram Fee Regulations" have not been changed. The recipient's name, title, ship name, coastal radio station name, or address for all domestic Chinese ship telegrams should be charged per word and are not subject to the charging method for the recipient's address and name specified in the "Domestic Telegraph Business Regulations." For example, in the telegram "{Commissioner Liu (36) Official Cabin Xin Ming Yantai}," the recipient's name, title, ship name, and coastal radio station name should be charged as thirteen words. For the recipient's ship radio station name in international ship telegrams, according to Articles 19, Sections 1 and 2 of the "International Telegraph Regulations," it should be allowed to be written together. For example, in the telegram "{Captain Watson, Chinaexportetxnhs}," Chinaexporterxnhs is the English ship name and ship radio station call sign of the Huada Ship. This recipient's ship radio station name can be counted as one word, regardless of the number of letters. However, if the ship name is written together in the text and it is proven to be the ship name without error, the maximum number of letters per word in foreign language ship telegrams is fifteen, and one word will be added for each additional letter. If the text is in code, the maximum number of letters per word is five. Except for international coded ship telegrams, which are allowed to be charged at 60% of the coded rate, domestic foreign language coded telegrams are charged at the full price and are not discounted. For example, "President Jackson" should be counted as two words in a foreign language telegram and four words in a coded telegram. Senders of ship telegrams should pay close attention to the above charging methods to avoid misunderstandings.

Nine-Province Long-Distance Telephone: Completion of the Beijing-Hankou Trunk Line Construction 229

Both East and West Sections are Now Open for Calls

The distance between Beijing and Hankou is approximately 1,215 kilometers. Jiujiang and Wuhu in between are the central hubs for commerce and culture in Central China. Nanchang and Huaining are important political and military strongholds. Therefore, the Beijing-Hankou trunk line is the most important project in the Ministry of Transportation and Communications' Nine-Province Long-Distance Telephone Project. After more than a year of effort, the project has been completed. The central station's power-assisted equipment is still being installed, and direct calls between Beijing and Hankou will soon be possible. The west section between Hankou, Nanchang, and Jiujiang, as well as the east section between Nanchang, Jiujiang, Huaining, Wuhu, and Nanjing, have all been opened for calls. The dates of the call openings and their prices are listed below:

Two Types of Public Welfare Telegrams Sponsored by the Ministry of Transportation and Communications 230

Hurricane Telegrams

During the hurricane season, coastal ship radio stations may have difficulty receiving hurricane warnings broadcast by the Central Meteorological Research Institute due to the distance. In order to ensure navigation safety, the Radio Administration of the Ministry of Transportation and Communications has requested the Central Meteorological Research Institute that, from June 1 to the end of October, when a hurricane warning is issued, in addition to broadcasting as usual, the warning should also be sent by telegram to the coastal radio stations in Shanghai, Fuzhou, Yantai, Tianjin, and Qingdao. Each of these stations will then follow the regulations for automatic warning signals in Section R of Article 22 of the International Radiotelegraph Convention, first sending twelve long dashes, and after a two-minute interval, sending the hurricane warning, in order to prepare for precautions. The Ministry of Transportation and Communications' Maritime Administration has also instructed the relevant maritime affairs bureaus to instruct the relevant ship radio stations to pay attention to receiving these warnings.

Flood Control Telegrams

Every summer in China, river levels rise greatly. If telegrams are not used to transmit information for prevention, there will inevitably be breaches extending for miles, resulting in vast floods. In order to support flood control efforts, the Ministry of Transportation and Communications has established a type of telegram called "Flood Control Telegrams." It is stipulated that from June 1 to the end of August, flood control telegrams sent by the Jianghan Engineering Bureau and its affiliated works offices, dike construction bureaus, flow measurement stations, and engineering offices, using the bureau's printed telegram paper, and telegrams sent by the bureau to the Southern Lian, National Economic Committee, Yangtze River Conservancy Commission, Shaanxi Water Conservancy Bureau, and the governments of all counties in Hubei Province with embankments, reporting on flood control, will be transmitted free of charge, but must be in clear language. The Ministry of Transportation and Communications has instructed the bureaus along the Yangtze River in Hubei Province to comply with this.

Personal Recommendation 231

Mr. Sun Keming of the Yantai Telegraph Bureau, drawing on his lifelong knowledge and experience, and referring to various Western books, has compiled a book titled "Solutions to Examination Questions for Wireless Telegraph Operators," totaling more than 200,000 words. The main text is divided into twelve chapters, with more than 540 questions and more than 100 illustrations. All wireless telegraph questions are covered, such as general theory, transmitter theory, application receivers, radio direction finding, storage batteries, motor generators, rectifiers, antennas, frequency measurement, convention regulations, shortwave broadcasting, wireless telephony, and aviation wireless, all are covered comprehensively. The book is currently being sold exclusively by the Zhongyong Wireless Electric Machinery Factory at 77 Lloyd Road, Shanghai. It will be published in mid-August. Those who pre-order before the end of July will receive a 50% discount, costing only one yuan (plus 0.13 yuan for registered postage).

Question and Answer Column 232

This publication has specially established a question and answer column. Members of the public who have unclear points regarding the procedures for sending and receiving telegrams and telephone calls, or regarding the telegraph regulations, or who have inquiries about general telegraph knowledge, are welcome to submit their questions, and this publication will provide answers.

Mr. Li Kezhi of Nanjing asks: What are half-price official telegrams? Full-price official telegrams? And bandit suppression military telegrams? Please provide detailed explanations.

(Answer) According to Article 8 of the "Domestic Telegraph Business Regulations," the following institutions' telegrams sent on official business are classified as official military telegrams and are charged at half the ordinary rate: 1. The Executive Committee, Supervisory Committee, and Central Political Conference of the Central Party Headquarters, and their directly affiliated associations and offices. 2. The National Government and its directly affiliated Yuan, Ministries, Committees, and Offices. 3. The Ministries and Committees directly under the Five Yuan. 4. Provincial Party Headquarters and municipal Party Headquarters directly under the Central Party Headquarters. 5. Provincial governments and municipal or local institutions directly under the Executive Yuan. 6. Military officers with the rank of division commander or independent brigade commander and above. 7. Commanders of naval fleets or important ports. 8. Air Force commanders. 9. Commissioners, representatives, or staff members dispatched by the above institutions (limited to those who send telegrams using the institution's printed telegram paper with the advance signature and seal of the responsible head of the institution). 10. Special Party Headquarters directly under the Central Party Headquarters (limited to important telegrams sent to the Central Party Headquarters using the Central Party Headquarters' printed telegram paper). 11. County and city Party Headquarters or district Party Headquarters directly under provincial Party Headquarters (limited to important telegrams sent to the Central Party Headquarters or the respective provincial Party Headquarters using the provincial Party Headquarters' printed telegram paper).

Full-price official telegrams refer to telegrams sent by responsible heads of other political and military institutions reporting on military affairs, disasters, or urgent matters related to local security. These telegrams are charged at the ordinary telegram rate (Chinese coded and clear language are priced the same) but are still transmitted in the order of official military telegrams.

Bandit suppression military telegrams refer to military telegrams sent by military institutions in combat or bandit suppression areas. A material fee of five jiao per hundred words is charged first (if the number of words is less than one hundred, it is counted as one hundred words), and the remaining unpaid fees are treated as arrears. The telegraph bureau fills out a form each month and sends it to the sending institution to be stamped, and then submits it to the Ministry of Transportation and Communications for verification.

Reading Club

Prospects for the First Volume of "New Youth" 233

— Wang Jian San

Receiving the latest issue of "New Youth" and seeing the index of the entire volume attached at the end, I realize that "New Youth" has been published for half a year now. Time flies so quickly!

Having read "New Youth" for half a year, as this first volume comes to an end and the second volume is about to begin, I would like to say a few words about this past volume, not as criticism, but merely as my impressions after reading it.

Frankly speaking, there are many magazines now, but if you want to find one that is suitable for students in upper elementary school and junior high school to read, it seems that there is none other than "New Youth." Although it can be said that this is because of my limited knowledge, it is undeniable that there are not many publications that are tailored to that level.

I believe that magazines are different from textbooks. The material in textbooks is dead, without temporal relevance, while magazines are different. They must publish the latest material to make sense. The magazines that ordinary students read now, apart from carrying some animals and plants that are appropriate for the season, do not care about anything else. "New Youth" is different. In addition to articles on animals and plants suitable for the season, such as "Adventure in the Stratosphere," "The French Maginot Line," "The World's Largest Ocean Liner: The Queen Mary," "The Aerial Palace: The Hindenburg," "The Total Solar Eclipse on June 19," etc., are all "new" and "youthful" materials with temporal relevance. Articles about animals and plants suitable for the season can be used this year or in future years, but topics like the ones mentioned above in "New Youth" would lose their timeliness if they were published next year or in the second half of the year. Therefore, the editors of "New Youth" have been able to pay attention to this word "new," which is something that other magazines have not done. Other materials are also not like other publications that indiscriminately select anything, as if "anything put in the basket is a vegetable." For example, on the two hundredth anniversary of Watt's birth, they talked about Watt; when Pavlov passed away, they introduced Pavlov's theories; when the Soviet Union was engaged in the "Stakhanov Movement," they introduced Stakhanov's history; on the fiftieth anniversary of the invention of aluminum, they talked about aluminum. This is not like the editors of other publications who talk about Watt when they have materials about Watt today, and publish the biography of Einstein tomorrow, as if it were a textbook where the materials in the third lesson can be moved to the fifth or tenth lesson without any problem. This is another area where "New Youth" magazine is superior to other magazines.

Usually, I hear a lot of criticism about magazines from friends. Many people recognize that since the publication of "New Youth," it has had a significant impact on other reading materials for young people. Therefore, some magazines not only imitate "New Youth" in many aspects of layout but also imitate it in many aspects of content. For example, the exhibition of Mr. Sheng Tao's articles is now included in several reading materials for young people; Mr. Yi Wen's "Youth Reading Room" is now also included in many reading materials for young people. However, this is superficial imitation, and the content is not as carefully selected as in "New Youth."

Regarding literary materials, other magazines mostly publish materials about cat brothers and dog brothers. This kind of material only caters to the low-level interests of children and is actually meaningless. "New Youth" magazine does not have this kind of material. Although it also publishes Mr. Sheng Tao's "Bird and Animal Language," the bird and animal language is definitely not as boring as cat brothers and dog brothers, so we cannot compare them. As for Mr. Sheng Tao's "Neighbors," which points out the impropriety of people's blind xenophobia, and Mr. Mao Dun's "Young Printing Worker," which points out the normal concept of young people towards occupations, these are things that cannot be seen in other publications.

China is a scientifically backward country, so magazines for ordinary students only publish game materials for science. "New Youth" is not like this. Science games and science interests are only used as filler materials, such as "Interesting Stories about Animals" in the eighth issue and "Aquatic Competition of Magnetic Needles" in the ninth issue, which are only filler. As for others, there are always two or three science articles in each issue, either in biology or in physics and chemistry, which not only provide theoretical explanations but also provide experimental methods. I think that if many other magazines also put in as much effort as "New Youth" in science, then although China's science is backward, students would not feel a headache when they see science subjects.

This volume of "New Youth," although only twelve thin issues, has very rich material, and the printing is very economical, with no wasted space. Moreover, except for the first issue, most of them are printed in size five font. As for "New Youth Lecture," it was printed in size six font later on. In this way, the space saved allows for the publication of one or two more articles, which is very suitable for readers. If we talk about the number of pages, perhaps other children's publications have more, but in terms of the number of words, "New Youth" has one or two times more than other children's publications.

I am not just flattering "New Youth." "New Youth" magazine naturally has its shortcomings. For example, some of the articles are relatively lacking in content. "The Hongkou Vegetable Market in Shanghai" does not describe the management of the vegetable market, nor does it bring out the suffering of vegetable vendors who are oppressed. I think the article only did the surface and did not write into the heart. "The Temple Fair at Jing'an Temple in Shanghai" does not have much social background. "About the China Traveling Theater Troupe" is mostly empty talk and somewhat like an advertisement for the traveling theater troupe. These cannot be considered minor flaws. However, it is not easy to compile a magazine, and it is not easy to demand that it be completely flawless. It seems a bit immoral for me to say a few sarcastic remarks on the sidelines. However, from the reader's point of view, we may as well demand more from it, although we know that the advantages of "New Youth" magazine outweigh these minor flaws.

Because "New Youth" is now the authority on all youth publications in China, I would like to say a few words about what I hope for in the second volume, in addition to briefly mentioning the content of the first volume above.

Of course, I hope that the second volume will maintain the above-mentioned advantages and eliminate the above-mentioned minor flaws. In terms of content, I hope to add more materials. For example, Mr. Zi Kai's "Art Stories" talks about painting. It would be best to also talk about music. Also, the turbulent international situation, such as "Abyssinia" and "Hitler's Elixir of Life," it would be best to have one or two articles of this kind in each issue. As for the publication aspect, it would be better if it could be published earlier. Because after we readers finish reading a new issue of the magazine, we immediately look forward to the early publication of the next issue. I think that many people may share this hope with me!

After reading the editor's postscript of the twelve issues of "New Youth," I know that the editors are also working hard to reform the second volume. Ah, well, I don't need to say anything more. I hope "New Youth" will always be the leader of general youth publications!

Why Write "The Resurrection of Philosophy"? 234

— Lin Zhu'yu

"The Resurrection of Philosophy" Published by Kaiming Bookstore, Actual Price 35 cents

If anyone were to be seen reading a philosophy book, people would invariably say, "Oh my, I never knew you were turning into a philosopher!" This is a very common and real occurrence that I frequently encounter. We can glean two layers of meaning from this statement.

First, philosophy has always been regarded as something sacred and unapproachable, said to be full of solemn language and incomprehensible theories. Reading it is like touching a hedgehog, with no good outcome. Therefore, those who study philosophy are seen as deities with three heads and six arms, possessing superhuman powers; or as old scholars with thick beards and wearing old-fashioned glasses, whose every sentence takes half an hour to understand. Of course, the person saying the former sentence is implicitly being sarcastic, mocking you for putting on airs, implying that becoming a philosopher is an impossible feat.

Second, in today's 20th century, science is particularly developed, as if everyone must become a scientist before they are satisfied. What is the point of philosophy? What is its use? It is always filled with insignificant phrases, and its meaning is shrouded in clouds, ambiguous and vague, impossible to grasp. Therefore, you see philosophy as fundamentally outdated, and you face the same bitter experience as a science student receiving a scornful look from a liberal arts student.

This is a correct assessment. Philosophy has always seemed very profound; you can pick up any philosophy book at random, and its thickness alone proves it. The depth of the language is also undeniable. Anyone who has translated philosophy books knows the difficulty, as terms like "intellect," "reason," "conscience," "idea," "reality," "concept," "image," "consciousness," "will"... are constantly used in different contexts, causing dizziness and mental fatigue after reading too much. As for the claim that philosophy is outdated, that is indeed true: scientific principles like gravity can be applied to inclined planes, but what use are philosophical concepts? Philosophy seems utterly useless. However, philosophy is necessary, and we should all read a few philosophy books. Philosophy is not difficult; when we read it, we experience a lingering aftertaste like eating olives, and it is easily broken down with just one bite. I firmly believe in this, which motivated me to write "The Resurrection of Philosophy" to prove that my words are not false. I have the following objectives:

1 The "Kaiming Youth Series" has everything else but lacks a philosophical work, making it incomplete. Therefore, I wrote "The Resurrection of Philosophy" to fill this gap, giving young people or any reader the opportunity to sample philosophy. A "general introduction" is most suitable for those who are new to or unclear about the subject, and "The Resurrection of Philosophy" has the nature of a "general introduction": it includes all the important philosophical questions, and each question provides ample hints and guidelines, so that future research can have a clear framework to grasp. However, this book differs from other ABCs or general introductions: (1) Although this book is a general introduction, after the general introduction, it offers fair criticism, so that the reader will not feel confused, and finally presents the author's views, which are supportive and do not interfere with other schools of thought, like icing on the cake. The reader can choose whatever they like: this style is probably not found in other books. (2) This book differs from other books in that it also contains historical records of philosophy. The history of philosophy is very important because it shows the formation process of each school of thought, tracing its origins and foundations, vividly presented. This is often overlooked in introductory books. Therefore, this book can be read as a general introduction to philosophy and as a history of philosophy, both of which provide a deeper understanding. It is very suitable as a textbook for high school philosophy electives. (3) This book has a precise dissection and narrative of Chinese philosophy. Ordinary philosophy books mostly focus on Western philosophy, and Chinese philosophy is not understood, which is a very tragic phenomenon. After reading this book and understanding Western philosophy, there is also a broad path to understanding Chinese philosophy. It is very suitable as a textbook and necessary for ordinary reading.

2 The content of philosophy is made very easy in this book because the main argument of this book is, "There is no philosophy, only the philosophy of life." Philosophy becomes profound because it focuses solely on cosmology and epistemology. This book argues that it is better to abandon cosmology and epistemology and focus on the philosophy of life. The philosophy of life is something everyone experiences, its meaning is simple, and everyone needs to understand it. If that is the case, wouldn't philosophy make people happy again, wouldn't it be "resurrected"? Even though that is said, this book still gives cosmology and epistemology a good position, offering thorough arguments, so that readers still have the necessary inherent knowledge.

3 The language used in this book strives to be concise, so that a thin book can include all the problems, but without making it "outline-like". Understanding is very easy, and there is no cumbersome and unclear language found in other philosophy books. After reading it, you can overcome the feeling that reading philosophy is a long journey. In addition, thoughtful examples are often cited to strengthen the impression, but without confusing the examples with the original meaning, so as to not lose the true meaning, like in some popular philosophy books where the examples overshadow the main point.

4 Philosophy and science have many interconnected relationships. People who study science should read philosophy, just as astronomy is a transformation of metaphysics and chemistry solves the organization of life, which all needs to be known. Therefore, this book mixes science and philosophy, so that those who study science and philosophy can have an academic connection, and so that those who study philosophy can know the true meaning of science. This is indeed a good method of learning, and should not be one-sided, but should be combined. Reading this book will naturally allow you to grasp the general situation of all knowledge and its relationships. Moreover, you will never see philosophy as a useless thing; on the contrary, it has the ability to help various sciences.

Finally, before the publication of this book, it was carefully proofread, and no misprints will occur. Also, the price is very low (only 35 cents, with a 30% discount during the special price period), making it affordable to buy. These are all things that the author is very happy about.

Editor's Note 235

Since the Ministry of Education issued instructions on the sale of textbooks and other books, the Shanghai Booksellers Association has held several meetings and decided to implement it from today. In addition to reducing the price of textbooks for sale, Kaiming Bookstore will also reduce the price of popular books to attract more widespread purchases, which is also good news for the reading community.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Notes

The Way Out for the Weak 236

— Shi Ji

Poverty and illness are the common fate of every worker in capitalist society.

In this common fate, there are only two paths in front of them: the strong take risks, while the weak are bound by invisible chains, forever suffering torment; or, unable to bear the long-term torment, they can only use their own hands to end their lives. And those who suffer torment, in the end, because they cannot bear the torment, also have only one path: death.

Or, they deliberately commit some "crime" and get locked up in prison, without having to bother to get an unimaginable amount of food, clothing and shelter. But what is the result? Relentless years flow by like water, and the black hair on their heads turns white, and the result is also death. Although they extend this thing called "life" a little longer than those who commit suicide, they are also causing their flesh to suffer more pain.

If a suffering and starving person is willing to endure that suffering, forever begging for a living in the mud, and has no lofty ideal in front of him, then I think it is better for him to die. To be at the mercy of others, whipped and abused, living like a pig in a stinking mud pit, can this really be considered "life"?

Although people cannot live entirely on "ideals," they cannot live without "ideals." If the thing thought of is never possible to realize, then it is a "fantasy," not an "ideal." The ideal is based on reality.

However, what the weak who are suffering from hunger and cold seem to universally lack is this, or, although they have "ideals," they build their "ideals" on others. They still long for life to "become" better than it is now, but they dare not fight against "life." (Think about it! Who made their "life" the way it is now?) They want others to improve their lives, and then they can enjoy it.

(There is naturally no such thing in the world.)

Let's take an example: a sixteen-year-old apprentice in a steel factory committed suicide. In his suicide note to his elder brother, he wrote, "Now, among the four of us, I rely entirely on my brother to make a name for himself, to avenge our parents, I hope you will not be sad.

He built the hope of "revenge" on his older brother, but he cowardly committed suicide, and even told his older brother not to be sad. Like the behavior of every "weak" person.

In this way, other than "death," the "weak" will never find their way out. Because they dare not fight hard against "life," and "life" will not let them go one step.

Where is the way out for the weak? I want to loudly ask the people who dare not fight with "life." Is "death" really the only way out for you?

The Story of Pigeons 237

— Green Leaf

(I want to write down some interesting stories about pigeons when I am lonely.)

When I was a child, my blind second uncle was my interesting companion. In the evening, I would put a few bamboo chairs with my eldest sister and brothers in the garden, and everyone would sit in pairs, playing clapping games or counting the stars in the sky. Because I was the youngest of them, they often ganged up to make fun of me, so I would play by myself. Thus, I could only talk to the lonely, blind second uncle, listening to him tell interesting stories about fireflies and rabbits, which often made me forget about them – my eldest sister and brothers – and yearn for the interesting things in the stories.

My blind second uncle once told me interesting stories about pigeons, and in my heart, I was full of excitement and yearning. Those interesting stories were painted red and blue. My blind second uncle was narrating his experiences raising pigeons. I often remember him constantly smiling, his eyes narrowed into a slit due to his chronic eye problem, and his lower jaw trembling as he spoke:

"Raising pigeons is so interesting. Even if they are hundreds of miles away, they still recognize their old home (Note)."

(But stories are just stories. When I was a child, I didn't understand anything, so I was easy to listen to and easy to forget. So after a few days, the yearning and excitement were gone. From my blind second uncle, I also heard about fish and cuckoos… many interesting stories.)

One morning, I heard a small, tinkling sound like jade leaves falling in the distance. I looked up and saw a dozen snow-white pigeons flying back and forth in the clear sky. Their silver wings glittered beautifully in the sunlight.

According to my blind second uncle, those were pigeons, and the small bells were clipped in the middle of their tails. When the wind blew, they would ring. So I remembered the beautiful stories about pigeons that my blind second uncle told me, and it made me think about raising pigeons myself.

Raising pigeons was unfamiliar to me, as I was still very young. But my blind second uncle readily agreed to handle everything. He built a house for the pigeons in the garden, and it only took him one day. It was something to see.

Finally, at Grandpa You Shun's house, I asked for a pair of young pigeons (that's what my blind second uncle told me to do. He said, "Adult pigeons will go back even after three or four years of raising, while young pigeons are like children and don't understand anything, so they are easy to raise.") I locked them in the newly built pigeon house, and I didn't care about anything else, "because I didn't know how to arrange things." I let my blind second uncle take care of the care and management alone. The next morning, I went to the garden with my eldest sister and brothers, and we could already see my blind second uncle busy adding food and water. Pigeons only eat some corn, wheat, green beans, and grains and other agricultural products, which we already had, so we didn't have to go to the street to buy them. We ran close to my blind second uncle, and while adding food, my blind second uncle said to us, "Wait for them to..."

Home
